# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've completed the research and created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings about graceful shutdown signal handling across the three Go services.

## Summary

I've identified **8 key Go source files** handling SIGTERM/SIGINT graceful shutdown across the three repositories:

### **Kubernetes/kubernetes:**
- Signal handler registration in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` with two-signal support
- Graceful termination orchestration in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` with multi-phase drain-before-stop pattern:
  1. Stop accepting new requests
  2. Drain non-long-running requests first
  3. Drain active watches with grace period
  4. Only then shutdown HTTP server

### **Grafana/grafana:**
- Signal handler in `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` with SIGHUP for log reload
- 30-second shutdown timeout enforced
- Clean cascade: signal → context timeout → service shutdown → timeout error handling

### **Prometheus/prometheus:**
- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` uses oklog/run.Group pattern for coordinated multi-component shutdown
- Critical cleanup ordering: discovery managers → rule manager → scrape manager → TSDB (TSDB closed AFTER scrapers stop writing)
- Ensures no writes to closed storage

All three services implement the pattern: **signal registration → context/timeout setup → drain connections → stop goroutines → cleanup resources**.

The answer is ready at `/workspace/answer.json`.

`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` contains `SetupSignalHandler()` and `SetupSignalContext()` functions that register for SIGTERM and SIGINT signals using `signal.Notify()`\\n- The handler creates a channel with capacity 2 to handle graceful shutdown: first signal cancels the context, second signal exits with code 1\\n- `signal_posix.go` defines `shutdownSignals` as `[]os.Signal{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}` for non-Windows platforms\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` defines `ShutdownTimeout` field (default 2*time.Second for HTTP Server shutdown after all requests drain)\\n- The timeout is respected in the `RunWithContext()` method which manages graceful termination\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering (Drain Before Stop):**\\n- The `RunWithContext()` method (lines 590-746) orchestrates a multi-phase graceful shutdown:\\n  1. Signal handler initiates shutdown when SIGTERM/SIGINT received\\n  2. Delay period elapses, then stops accepting new requests via `NotAcceptingNewRequest` signal\\n  3. Non-long-running requests are drained first (`NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup.Wait()`)\\n  4. Active watches are drained with a grace period (`ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod`)\\n  5. Only after both drain channels signal completion does the HTTP server shutdown\\n  6. Pre-shutdown hooks run for cleanup (e.g., deregistering from endpoints)\\n  7. Audit backend is shutdown after requests drain\\n  8. Finally, HTTP listeners and server stop\\n\\n**Sample Controller Pattern:**\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` provides a reusable `SetupSignalHandler()` pattern with the same two-signal approach\\n\\n### Grafana/grafana\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` has `listenToSystemSignals()` function that registers:\\n  - SIGHUP for log reload functionality\\n  - SIGTERM/SIGINT for graceful shutdown via `signal.Notify()`\\n- The handler runs in a goroutine and listens in a select loop for different signals\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` creates a context with 30-second timeout for shutdown: `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)`\\n- `pkg/server/server.go` implements the `Shutdown()` method that respects this timeout and handles shutdown failures\\n- `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` implements gRPC-specific shutdown with `GracefulShutdownTimeout` configuration (line 195)\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering:**\\n- `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` signal handler (lines 148-170):\\n  1. Signal received (SIGTERM/SIGINT)\\n  2. Create shutdown context with timeout\\n  3. Call `s.Shutdown(ctx, reason)`\\n- `pkg/server/server.go` Shutdown() method (lines 155-172):\\n  1. Stops background services via `managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, \\\"shutdown\\\")`\\n  2. Waits for context to complete or timeout\\n  3. Returns error if shutdown times out\\n- `pkg/services/grpcserver/service.go` gRPC shutdown (lines 184-199):\\n  1. Initiates graceful stop in goroutine\\n  2. Waits for graceful stop to complete OR timeout\\n  3. Forces stop if timeout exceeded\\n\\n### Prometheus/prometheus\\n\\n**Signal Handler Registration:**\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go` lines 1154-1177 register SIGTERM and SIGINT handlers using `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)`\\n- Uses the `github.com/oklog/run.Group` pattern for managing multiple goroutines with coordinated shutdown\\n- Termination handler is the first actor in the run.Group, establishing graceful shutdown flow\\n\\n**Shutdown Timeout:**\\n- Implicit timeout handling through `run.Group`: when one actor stops, the cleanup function (second argument to `g.Add()`) is called\\n- Each component's cleanup function handles resource release with appropriate timing\\n\\n**Cleanup Ordering (Critical Drain Sequence):**\\nThe `cmd/prometheus/main.go` main() function demonstrates careful shutdown ordering (lines 1150-1600+):\\n\\n1. **Signal Handler (lines 1153-1177):** Registers SIGTERM/SIGINT, initiates shutdown flow\\n2. **Discovery Managers (lines 1179-1204):** Stop scrape and notify discovery managers first to prevent new targets\\n3. **Rule Manager (lines 1207-1219):** Stops before stopping scrape manager to avoid false positives\\n4. **Scrape Manager (lines 1222-1243):** Stopped AFTER rule manager but BEFORE TSDB closure - critical ordering with comment: \\\"Scrape manager needs to be stopped before closing the local TSDB so that it doesn't try to write samples to a closed storage\\\"\\n5. **Tracing Manager (lines 1246-1258):** Stops concurrent with other managers\\n6. **Reload Handler (lines 1261-1343):** Waits for in-progress reloads before stopping\\n7. **Configuration Loading (lines 1346-1374):** Initial config loader stops\\n8. **TSDB/Storage (lines 1376-1435):** Storage closed AFTER all managers that write to it are stopped\\n9. **Remote Storage (cleanup functions):** Closed after scrape manager stops\\n10. **Web Handler (lines 1497+):** Web interface shutdown last\\n\\nThe run.Group pattern ensures that:\\n- Each component's Run() function blocks until its cancel channel closes\\n- The cleanup function for each component is called when the group is interrupted\\n- Cleanup functions can stop dependencies in proper order\\n- All components complete their cleanup before the program exits\\n\\n### Key Patterns Across All Three Services\\n\\n1. **Signal Registration Pattern:** All three use `signal.Notify()` with SIGTERM and SIGINT as primary shutdown signals\\n2. **Context-Based Cancellation:** Both Kubernetes and Grafana use Go contexts with timeouts; Prometheus uses run.Group with cleanup callbacks\\n3. **Two-Signal Handling:** Kubernetes and sample-controller explicitly handle a second signal to force exit\\n4. **Graceful Drain Ordering:** All three implement drain-before-stop patterns:\\n   - Kubernetes: drain requests \u2192 drain watches \u2192 shutdown HTTP \u2192 cleanup\\n   - Grafana: stop services \u2192 respect timeout \u2192 error on overflow\\n   - Prometheus: stop scrapers \u2192 drain storage writes \u2192 shutdown TSDB\\n5. **Timeout Management:** All specify explicit shutdown timeouts (Kubernetes: 2-30s, Grafana: 30s, Prometheus: implicit via goroutine cleanup)\"\n}\n",
